Dialectic -- Jadal
intermediate
10 min
Defining Munazara: Components and Purpose
Author defines munazara as mutual refutation between sa'il and mu'allil to manifest truth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the genus and differentia in the definition of munazara and distinguish it from jadal.

Core Idea
Munazara is a truth-seeking refutation, not a silencing contest.

In this passage, the author lays out the technical definition of munazara (dialectical debate). He gives its genus (mudafa'a, mutual refutation) and its differentia (between sa'il and mu'allil for manifesting truth). Understanding this definition is crucial because it sets munazara apart from mere disputation (jadal), which aims at silencing the opponent. As you work through the lesson, you will learn to parse the definition into its essential components and apply the same analytical lens to other definitions in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being defined. In this passage, the author defines 'munazara' (المناظرة) in the technical sense of Islamic logic.
2
Extract the genus
The genus is 'mudafa'a' (المدافعة), meaning mutual refutation or repelling. This places munazara in the broader category of argumentative exchanges.
The author notes that mudafa'a is the common element between munazara and other dispute forms.
3
Identify the differentia
The specific difference lies in the parties (al-sā'il and al-mu'allil) and the purpose (izhār al-ḥaqq, manifesting truth). The sa'il demolishes the judgment; the mu'allil defends it.
The purpose is what distinguishes munazara from jadal.
4
Distinguish munazara from jadal
Jadal (الجدل) is refutation for silencing the opponent, regardless of truth. Munazara aims at confirming what is true. The same exchange can be munazara for one party and jadal for the other.
This distinction is crucial for evaluating actual debates in Islamic sciences.
5
Apply the definitional model
Practice by identifying the genus and differentia in other technical definitions from Islamic logic, such as 'qiyas' or 'istidlal'.

الشخصين المعلل والسائل فلا يحتاج إلى التفسير الآتى فيحمل على المعنى الأعم فيرد عليه أن التعريف صادق على المدافعة فى المحكوم عليه وبه مع أنها ليست بمناظرة . وبجاب بأن المراد من دفع السائل دفعه قول المعلل في النسبة ودفع قول السائل فيها ( ليظهر الحق ) من الظهور : أى لتحصيل ظهور الحق أو من الاظهار، وهو الظاهر الموافق لما اشتهر ، فالضمير راجع إلى المذكور التزاما فى المدافعة فافهم، وظهور الحق أعم من أن يكون في يده أو فى يد خصمه وأن يكون وحده أو مع شيء آخر فلا يرد عليه أنه غير صادق على المناظرة التي يظهر الحق في بد خصمه والتي يقصد فيها غلط الخصم مع ظهور الحق مطلقا، وهو احتراز عن الجدل فانه مدافعة لاسكات الخصم لأن كلا من المجادلين يريد حفظ مقاله وهدم مقال خصمه سواء كان حقا أو باطلا. قال المحقق التفتازاني في شرح العقائد الحق هو الحكم المطابق للواقع يطلق على الأقوال والعقائد والأديان والمذاهب باعتبار اشتمالها على ذلك ويقابله الباطل ، وأنها الصدق فقد شاع في الأقوال خاصة ويقابله الكذب : وقد يفرق بينهما بأن المطابقة تعتبر فى الحق من جانب الواقع ، وفي الصدق من جانب الحكم ؛ فمعنى صدق الحكم مطابقته للمواقع ، ومعنى حقيته مطابقة الواقع إياه اهـ ولما كانت المدافعة لاظهار الحق شاملة لمدافعة الشخصين سواء كانا سائلين أو غيرهما بادر إلى التفسير بقوله ( أعنى دفع السائل ) وهو الناصب نفسه لهدم الحكم فيشمل المنوع الثلاثة مطلقا (قول الملل) وهو الناصب نفسه لبيان الحكم ، والقول أعم من المقدمة والدليل والمدعى ) ودفع المعلل قول السائل ) والأخصر أن يقال هى المدافعة من السائل والمعلل إظهارا للحق . ولما كان دفع المعلل موقوفا على دفع السائل قدم دفعه على دفعه أو الانتظار أو النظر بالبصيرة ، وهو مشترك بين المعنيين الحركات التخيلية وترتيب أمور معلومة لا تأدى إلى مجهول. والأول يعم المنع دون الثاني، ولا يخفى مناسبة كل من هذه المعانى المعنى العرقي ) في العرف ( الخاص ) هى المدافعة ) . ومناكرة المتباينين ليست بمدافعة فيخرج عن التعريف ليظهر الحق) أى لاظهار الثابت في الواقع ، أو ليظهره سواء قصد إسكات الخصم أولا فيخرج الجدل فلذا قال في الحاشية احتراز عن الجدل فانه المدافعة لإسكات الخصم ، ومعناه أن كلا من المجادلين يقصد حفظ مقاله سواء كان حقا أو باطلا ويريد هدم مقال خصمه سواء كان حقا أو باطلا انتهى . فاذا قصد أحد الخصمين إظهار الحق والآخر إسكات الخصم فالمدافعة التي بينهما مناظرة بالنسبة إلى الأول وجدل بالنسبة إلى الثانى فاعرف وأما الاعتراض على التعريف و التقسيم والعبارة مع توجيهه ، فدخل فى التعريف الكون المطابقة وعدمها متصورا فيها باعتبار الشروط ستعرفه فينعكس لكن إخراج الأخير عن الأقسام لانحطاط رتبته لكن متعلقه لفظا لا معنى ؛ والمدافعة في عرفهم موضوع لدفع كل من الملل والسائل قول الآخر فلا ينتقض التعريف بمجادلة رجلين ادعى كل منهما غلبته على الآخر فدفع كل الآخر لإظهار صدق مقاله ، ولذا قال ( أعنى دفع السائل قول المعلل ودفع المعلل قول السائل ) فلا يعترض بأن العام لا دلالة له على الخاص باحدى
In the sense of sight, or waiting, or thought, or confrontation, and the aspects of appropriateness are not hidden. (In custom it is mutual refutation). It is the exchange of speech between two persons, each intending to correct his own statement and invalidate his companion's statement, as was said. If the two persons are intended to be the mu'allil and the sa'il, then the following explanation is not needed, so it is interpreted in the more general sense. Then it is objected that the definition applies to refutation concerning the judged and that by which it is judged, while it is not a munazara. And the answer is that what is intended by the sa'il's refutation is his refutation of the mu'allil's statement regarding the relation, and the mu'allil's refutation of the sa'il's statement therein, (to manifest the truth) from 'zuhur': i.e., to achieve the manifestation of truth, or from 'izhar', and it is the apparent meaning in line with what is well-known. So the pronoun refers implicitly to what was mentioned in the refutation, so understand. The manifestation of truth is more general, whether it be in his hand or in the hand of his opponent, and whether it be alone or with something else. So it is not objected that it does not apply to a munazara in which truth appears in the hand of the opponent, or in which the silencing of the opponent is intended while truth appears absolutely. This is a safeguard against jadal, for it is a refutation for silencing the opponent, because each of the disputants wants to preserve his own statement and demolish the statement of his opponent, whether it be right or wrong. Al-Muhaqqiq al-Taftazani said in Sharh al-'Aqa'id: Truth is a judgment conforming to reality; it is applied to statements, beliefs, religions, and sects by virtue of their inclusion of that, and its opposite is falsehood. And it is veracity, which is common especially in statements, and its opposite is falsehood. Sometimes a distinction is made between them: conformity is considered in truth from the side of reality, and in veracity from the side of the judgment. So the meaning of a judgment being true is its conformity to reality, and the meaning of its being truthful is reality's conformity to it. End. And since the refutation for manifesting truth includes the refutation of two persons whether they be questioners or others, he hastened to interpret with his saying: (Meaning the refutation of the sa'il), who is the one who sets himself up to demolish the judgment, so it includes the three types of preventer absolutely; (the statement of the mu'allil), who is the one who sets himself up to explain the judgment, and 'statement' is more general than premise, proof, and claim; (and the mu'allil's refutation of the sa'il's statement). The shortest is to say: It is the refutation between the sa'il and the mu'allil for the manifestation of truth. And since the mu'allil's refutation depends on the sa'il's refutation, he presented his refutation before his. Or waiting, or insight, which is shared between two meanings: imaginative movements and the arrangement of known matters leading to an unknown. The first includes prevention without the second. The appropriateness of each of these meanings to the technical meaning is not hidden. In the specific custom: It is mutual refutation. The mutual avoidance of two disparate things is not refutation, so it exits the definition. To manifest truth: i.e., to manifest what is established in reality, or to manifest it whether or not the silencing of the opponent is intended; then jadal exits. Hence he said in the gloss: A safeguard against jadal, for it is refutation for silencing the opponent, meaning that each of the disputants intends to preserve his own statement whether right or wrong, and wants to demolish the statement of his opponent whether right or wrong. End. So if one of the two opponents intends to manifest truth and the other intends to silence the opponent, then the refutation between them is munazara relative to the first and jadal relative to the second. Know that. As for the objection to the definition, division, and expression with its orientation, then it enters the definition: the state of conformity and non-conformity is conceivable therein by virtue of conditions you will know, so it is reversed, but the last is excluded from the divisions due to its low rank, but its concern is verbal not meaningful. And 'refutation' in their custom is used for the repelling of each of the mu'allil and sa'il of the other's statement, so the definition is not invalidated by the dispute of two men each claiming his victory over the other, so each repels the other to manifest the truth of his statement. Hence he said: (Meaning the sa'il's refutation of the mu'allil's statement and the mu'allil's refutation of the sa'il's statement). So it is not objected that the general does not indicate the specific by one of the three indications.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage defines munazara (debate) in the technical sense of the logicians. The author begins by noting that the word 'nazar' has several linguistic meanings (sight, waiting, thought, confrontation) and then states that in custom it means mutual refutation (mudafa'a). He then expands on the definition: it is an exchange of speech between two persons, each aiming to correct his own statement and invalidate the other's. However, this preliminary definition is refined to specify the roles: the sa'il (objector) and the mu'allil (respondent). The sa'il is the one who sets out to demolish the judgment, and the mu'allil is the one who sets out to explain the judgment. The purpose of this mutual refutation is to manifest truth (izhar al-haqq). The author addresses an objection that the definition might apply to refutation about the thing judged and the criterion of judgment, which is not a munazara, but answers that the intended refutation is specifically about the relation (al-nisba) between the two statements. The definition is distinguished from jadal (disputation) by its purpose: in munazara, the aim is truth, whereas in jadal, the aim is to silence the opponent, regardless of truth. The author quotes al-Taftazani to clarify the meaning of haqq (truth) as a judgment matching reality. The passage then explains that the definition implicitly includes the four causes (formal, material, efficient, final) through its components. The author also addresses potential objections about the general term 'person' and clarifies that the definition is precise by specifying the two parties. Finally, he notes that the general term does not imply the specific without additional indication, so the definition stands.

المدافعة
السائل

الجدل

A) The presence of two parties
B) The aim of manifesting truth (izhar al-haqq)

Key Takeaway
Munazara is defined by its genus (mutual refutation), its parties (sa'il and mu'allil), and its purpose (manifesting truth), which together distinguish it from jadal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the following excerpt from a debate on the definition of riba: 'The sa'il objects that the mu'allil's analogy is flawed because the 'illah is not effective.' Identify which part corresponds to the sa'il's refutation and which to the mu'allil's response. Then decide whether the exchange qualifies as munazara or jadal based on the stated purpose.
?

Critique of the Standard Definition of Munazara
Author critiques the famous definition of munazara and identifies its deficiencies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four causal components embedded in the definition of munazara and evaluate the shortcomings of the standard definition of dialectical debate.

Core Idea
A definition of dialectical debate must cover all cases—including sheer prevention—otherwise it fails.

The author critiques the famous definition of munazara (dialectical debate) as 'inspection with insight from both sides concerning the relationship between two things.' He finds it deficient because it does not apply to debates involving sheer prevention. He then reveals a deeper structure: the definition actually contains the four Aristotelian causes. This lesson will guide you through his analysis and help you assess definitions critically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the criticized definition
Find the definition of munazara as 'inspection with insight from both sides' (النظر بالبصيرة من الجانبين في النسبة بين الشيئين). Note its components: inspection (nazar), insight (basira), both sides, relationship between two things.
This is the standard definition from earlier texts, often attributed to the early logicians.
2
Understand the objection regarding sheer prevention
The author argues the definition fails for debates where one side is sheer prevention (منع مجرد). Why? Because 'inspection' implies thought (fikr), which is the arrangement of knowns to arrive at an unknown, whereas sheer prevention is not such an arrangement—it is simply a negation without constructive reasoning.
This shows the definition is too narrow.
3
Extract the four causes from the author's alternative
In his preferred conceptualization, look for: formal cause (mudafa'a – mutual defense), material cause (the relationship understood from mudafa'a), efficient cause (mu'allil and sa'il – the participants), and final cause (izhar al-haqq – manifesting truth). The author states three causes are explicit and one implicit.
This causal analysis provides a more comprehensive framework.
4
Assess the reasons for departure from the famous definition
The author lists several reasons: the famous definition is ambiguous (inspection can be mere attention), too general (includes teacher-student scenarios), redundant (insight adds nothing), or fails to capture the verbal interactive essence of debate. Note how each reason strengthens the case for his preferred definition.
This step trains you to evaluate definitions critically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن هذا التعريف لا يصدق على المدافعة بين صاحب التعريف وناقضه وبين صاحب التقسيم وناقضه ؛ وإن كان صادقاً على دفع السائل فيهما فقط ، اللهم إلا أن يحمل المملل والسائلة على المعنى الأعم الشامل لصاحب التعريف والتقسيم وناقضهما ، أو يجعل المدافعة فهما فرعا للمدافعة فى الدليل والمدعى فليتأمل ، ومن لطائف هذا التعريف أنه مشتمل على العلل الأربع فالمدافعة إشارة إلى العملة الصورية والنسبة المفهومة من المدافعة إلى العملة المادية والمملل والسائل إلى العملة الفاعلية وإظهار الحق إلى العلة الغائية ، فعلى ما ذكرنا تكون العلل الثلاث مذكورة بالمطابقة ، والنسبة المفهومة من المدافعة والقول مذكورة التزاماً ، وعدل عن التعريف المشهور وهو النظر بالبصيرة من الجانبين فى النسبة بين الشيئين إظهارا للصواب لورود السؤال عليه بأنه غير صادق على المناظرة التى أحد طرفيها منع مجرد، لأن المراد من النظر هو الفكر ، وهو ترتيب أمور معلومة للتأدى إلى مجهول والمنع ليس كذلك . وإن أجيب عنه بأن الفكر ههنا بمعنى توجه النفس والتفاتها نحو المجهول ، وبأنه صادق على مخالفة المتفكرين في النسبة من غير تكلم، ونظر العلم والمتعلم في أحد طرفي الحكم مع أن كلا منهما ليس بمناظرة : وإن أجيب عنه أيضا بأن المراد من الجانبين الملل والسائل لاختصاص الجانبين بهما بحسب متفاهم عرفهم ، وإن كان أعم بحسب مفهوم اللغة أو لدفع توهم من يتوهم أنه ليس للمناظرة تعريف سوى هذا التعريف أو للتنبيه على جواز تعدد التعريف لشيء واحد أو للتنشيط أو للتنبيه على أن مدار المناظرة على المخاطبة والمدافعة نص فيها بخلاف النظر بالبصيرة أو لغير ذلك .
And know that this definition does not apply to the mutual defense between the definer and his objector, nor between the divider and his objector; although it applies to the repulsion of the questioner in both only, unless the term 'mumallil' and 'sa'il' are taken in the general sense that includes the definer, divider, and their objectors, or the mutual defense is made a branch of the defense in the evidence and the claim, so let it be pondered. Among the subtleties of this definition is that it includes the four causes: the mutual defense indicates the formal cause, the relationship understood from the mutual defense indicates the material cause, the 'mumallil' and 'sa'il' indicate the efficient cause, and manifesting the truth indicates the final cause. Thus, according to what we mentioned, three causes are mentioned explicitly, and the relationship understood from the mutual defense and the statement is mentioned implicitly. He departed from the famous definition, which is 'inspection with insight from both sides concerning the relationship between two things,' to manifest correctness, because an objection arose against it that it does not apply to a debate in which one of the two sides is sheer prevention, because what is meant by 'inspection' is thought, which is the arrangement of known matters to arrive at the unknown, whereas prevention is not like that. Even if it is answered that thought here means the direction of the soul and its attention towards the unknown, and that it applies to the disagreement of the thinkers concerning the relationship without speech, and the consideration of the teacher and student concerning one of the two sides of the judgment, although neither of them is a debate; and even if it is also answered that what is meant by 'the two sides' is the 'mumallil' and 'sa'il', because the two sides are specific to them according to the understanding of their convention, even if it is more general according to the linguistic sense, or to repel the notion of one who thinks that there is no definition of debate other than this definition, or to indicate the permissibility of multiple definitions for one thing, or for stimulation, or to indicate that the basis of debate is verbal address and mutual defense, which is explicit in it, unlike inspection with insight, or for other reasons.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is a critical examination of a well-known definition of munazara (dialectical debate). The author points out that the definition does not cover all instances of mutual defense, specifically between the definer/divider and their objectors. He then discusses the four causes embedded in this definition: the formal cause is the mutual defense, the material cause is the relationship understood from it, the efficient cause is the participants (the 'mumallil' and 'sa'il'), and the final cause is manifesting truth. The author then explains why he departed from the famous definition, which defines munazara as 'inspection with insight from both sides concerning the relationship between two things.' He lists several objections and responses, showing that the famous definition fails in cases where one side is simply preventing, or when the term 'inspection' is ambiguous. He also argues that the term 'insight' is redundant, and that 'both sides' is too general. The author concludes by listing possible reasons for his departure, such as avoiding misconceptions or emphasizing the verbal interactive nature of debate.

Key Terms
المدافعة (al-mudafa'a): Mutual defense or argumentative exchange between two parties in a debate.
المعلل (al-mu'allil): The one who provides a proof or justification; the respondent in a debate. [Note: In other contexts, 'mu'allil' may mean one who gives a cause ('illa).]
السائل (al-sa'il): The questioner or objector in a debate. [Note: Stable across the tradition.]
النظر بالبصيرة (al-nazar bi al-basira): Inspection with insight; a mental consideration of the relationship between two things. [Note: This is the standard definition of munazara in earlier texts; author critiques it.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, which of the four causes is NOT explicitly mentioned in the definition of munazara?
A) The formal cause (mudafa'a)
B) The material cause (the relationship understood from mudafa'a)
C) The efficient cause (mu'allil and sa'il)
D) The final cause (izhar al-haqq)

Key Takeaway
A robust definition of dialectical debate must account for its causal structure and avoid ambiguities that exclude valid forms of interaction like sheer prevention.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Take the definition of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in usul al-fiqh: 'Applying the ruling of a known case to an unknown case due to shared effective cause ('illa).' Identify the four causes (material, formal, efficient, final) in this definition, following the author's method in the lesson.
?
2. Consider a debate where one participant simply denies a premise without providing a counterargument. Does this fit the definition of munazara as 'inspection from both sides'? Explain why or why not using the author's objection about sheer prevention.

The Subject Matter of Munazara: Complete Informative Relations
Author introduces munazara and excludes mufrad and insha'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether a given expression (mufrad, insha', or khabar) is suitable for munazara based on its relation type.

Core Idea
Munazara only deals with truth-apt propositions, not isolated terms or performatives.

In this lesson, we explore the foundational condition for any dialectical debate: the expression must convey a complete informative relation (nisba tamma khabariyya). The author distinguishes between simple terms (mufrad), performatives (insha'), and informative propositions (khabar), explaining why only the latter is directly debatable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of expression
Determine whether the expression is a single word (mufrad), a performative utterance (insha'), or a declarative statement (khabar).
2
Check for a complete relation (nisba tamma)
Ask: Does the expression have a subject and predicate? Does it claim something that can be true or false?
3
Assess informativity (khabariyya)
If the expression has a complete relation but is performative (e.g., a command), consider if it implies an informative claim (hukman). The author acknowledges such cases are debatable in effect.
4
Apply to munazara
Based on your analysis, decide whether the expression is a valid subject for debate. Simple terms and pure performatives (without informative implication) are excluded.

والانشاء ففيه تغليب ) لا يمكن فيهما المناظرة ) إذ متعلق المناظرة هي النسبة التامة الخبرية حقيقة أو حكما والمفرد ليس له نسبة أصلا والانشاء وإن كان له نسبة تامة لكنها ليست بخبرية والمراد أن المناظرة لا تتعاق بالنسبة التامة المفهومة من الانشاء بالمطابقة فلا ينافيه تعلقها بالنسبة التامة الخبرية. اللازمة لجميع الإنشاء وأما السؤال بمعنى الاستفسار فليس داخلا في المناظرة وإذا لم يمكن المناظرة فيها ) فنضع ثلاثة أبواب ( كل باب لبيان وظائف واحد من الأمور الثلاثة . فان قلت الواجب أن يقول أربعة أبواب لأن غير الأخيرين أربعة أشياء . قلت المركب الناقص إن كان قيدا للقضية فهو تصديق معنى ، وإلا فلا يجرى فيه المناظرة كالمفرد والانشاء . الباب الأول : فى التعريف أي في بيان الأبحاث المتعلقة بالتعريف لأن المصنف بصدد بيان وظائف التعريف ويان أحوال التعريف مذكور بالتبع وهو إما لفظى أو تنبهي أو حقيق، واللفظى ما يقصد به تفسير مدلول اللفظ والتنبهي ما يقصد به إحضار صورة مخزونة في خزينة الخيال بلا نجم إلى كسب جديد والحقيقي ما يستلزم تصوره تصور الشيء وهو إماحد تام وهو ما يتركب من الجنس والفصل القريبين وإما حد ناقص وهوما يتركب من الجنس البعيد و الفصل القريب وإما رسم تام وهو المركب من الجنس ) ولنشرع فى بيان المناظرة على تقدير عدم النقل ) عن الشخص والكتاب فاحفظها تكن من أولى الألباب ( واعلم أن الأخيرين ) وهما المفرد والإنشاء ( يمكن فيهما المناظرة ) إذ متعلق المناظرة : هى النسبة التامة الخيرية حقيقة أو حكما كما عرفت إلا أنها لما لم تحقق إلا بتحقق الطرفين يعدون محل المناظرة المجموع والمفرد ليس له نسبة أصلا و الانشاء له نسبة تامة لكنها ليست بخبرية لا حقيقة ولا حكما ، وفيه نظر لأن الانشاء قد يكون له نسبة تامة خبرية حكما كما إذا قلت حد حين قراءته شيئا لا تقرا القرآن محدثا فكأنك ادعيت كون المقروء قرآنا وكون القارئ محدثا وعدم جواز قراءة المحدث القرآن فله أن يمنع كون المقروء قرآنا وكونه محدثا وعدم جواز قراءة المحدث قرآنا ( فنضع ثلاثة أبواب ( لبيان المناظرة الجارية في الثلاثة الأول وهي التعريف والتقسيم والتصديق . قال في الحاشية: إن قلت الواجب أربعة أبواب قلت المركب الناقص إن كان لأحد فيدا للقضية فهو تصديق معنى وإن لم يكن قيدا فلا يجرى فيه المناظرة كالمفرد والانشاء اه . وقد عرفت الكلام فى الانشاء وكذا الكلام في قيده. إن قلت إن التعريف والتقسم من قبيل التصورات فليس لها نسبة تامة خبرية لا حقيقة ولا حكما بل صورة فلا يمكن فيهما المناظرة . قلت نعم إنهما من قبيل التصورات لكن لما كان كل منهما مشروطا بشروط كانت نسبتهما تامة خبرية حكما فتأمل . ( الباب الأول ) فى بيان المناظرة الجادة ( في التعريف ) الحقيقي وهو ما يستلزم بطريق النظر امتياز الشيء بجميع أفراده عن جميع ما عداه عند المتأخر ومطلقا عند
(And we shall begin) i.e., it is incumbent upon us to begin, and it is permissible that the lam is for inception in explaining munazara, which is the description of the two disputants on the assumption of non-transmission. He gave it precedence over the former because of its prevalence and the abundance of its investigations. (And know that the last two) i.e., the simple and the performative (here there is predominance) (munazara is not possible in them) because the subject matter of munazara is the complete informative relation, in reality or in effect; the simple has no relation at all, and the performative, although it has a complete relation, it is not informative. And the intention is that munazara does not concern the complete relation understood from the performative by primary signification; thus it does not conflict with its being concerned with the complete informative relation necessary for all performatives. As for the question in the sense of inquiry, it is not included in munazara. And since munazara is not possible in them, we lay down three chapters—each chapter for explaining the functions of one of the three matters. For if you say: it is necessary to say four chapters, because besides the last two there are four things. I say: the deficient compound, if it is a qualifier of the proposition, is a tasdiq in meaning; otherwise, munazara does not apply to it, like the simple and the performative. Chapter One: On Definition, i.e., in explaining the investigations related to definition, because the author is intending to explain the functions of definition, and the states of definition are mentioned by way of subsidiary. And it is either verbal, or attention-drawing, or real. The verbal is that by which the interpretation of the meaning of the word is intended; the attention-drawing is that by which the retrieval of a form stored in the treasury of imagination is intended without attaining to new acquisition; and the real is that whose conception entails the conception of the thing. And it is either a complete definition, which is composed of the proximate genus and difference; or a deficient definition, which is composed of the remote genus and the proximate difference; or a complete description, which is composed of the genus... (And we shall begin in explaining munazara on the assumption of non-transmission) from the person and the book, so memorize it, you will be among those of understanding. (And know that the last two), which are the simple and the performative, (munazara is possible in them) because the subject matter of munazara is the complete informative relation, in reality or in effect, as you have known, except that since it is not realized except by the realization of the two sides, they consider the locus of munazara to be the whole. And the simple has no relation at all, and the performative has a complete relation but it is not informative, neither in reality nor in effect. And there is a consideration: because the performative may have a complete informative relation in effect, as when you say, 'Someone, when he reads something, do not read the Qur'an while in a state of hadath (ritual impurity)' as if you claimed that what is read is the Qur'an, and the reader is in a state of hadath, and the impermissibility of the hadath-person reading the Qur'an; so he can deny that what is read is the Qur'an, and that he is in a state of hadath, and the impermissibility of the hadath-person reading the Qur'an. (So we lay down three chapters) for explaining the munazara that takes place in the first three: namely definition, division, and assent. He said in the gloss: If you say: it is necessary to have four chapters, I say: the deficient compound, if it is a qualifier of the proposition, is a tasdiq in meaning; but if it is not a qualifier, munazara does not apply to it, like the simple and the performative. And you have known the discussion about the performative and similarly the discussion about its qualifier. If you say: definition and division are from the category of conceptions, so they have no complete informative relation, neither in reality nor in effect, but rather a form, so munazara is not possible in them. I say: Yes, they are from the category of conceptions, but since each of them is conditioned by conditions, their relation becomes a complete informative relation in effect, so consider. (Chapter One) in explaining serious munazara (in real definition), which is that which necessarily entails, by way of examination, the distinguishing of the thing with all its individuals from all other than it, according to the later scholars, and absolutely according to... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a methodological preface to the section on munazara (dialectical debate). The commentator explains that munazara deals with complete informative relations (nisba tamma khabariyya). The simple expression (mufrad) has no relation, so it cannot be debated. The performative (insha') has a complete relation but it is not informative (khabari), so it too is excluded from munazara, unless it implies an informative claim (as when a prohibition implies an assertion of impermissibility). There is an apparent contradiction: first it says munazara is not possible in the last two, then later it says it is possible. The commentator reconciles by pointing out that performatives can have informative import in effect (hukman). The author then states that we lay down three chapters (abwab) for the first three categories (definition, division, and assent) because the fourth (deficient compound) is either a qualifier to a proposition (making it a tasdiq) or not a subject of debate. The first chapter is on definition (ta'rif). Definition is divided into verbal (lafzi), attention-drawing (tanbihi), and real (haqiqi). The verbal merely explains the meaning of a word; the attention-drawing retrieves a stored image; the real definition yields the conception of the thing. Real definition is further subdivided into complete definition (hadd tamm: proximate genus + proximate difference), deficient definition (hadd naqis: remote genus + proximate difference), and complete description (rasm tamm: composed of genus + proximate? Actually it says 'composed of genus' and cuts off). The passage also discusses the seeming objection that definition and division are conceptual (tasawwuri) and not informative propositions, so they would not be suitable for munazara. The answer is that they are conditioned by requirements (shurut) that make them effectively informative (tamma khabariyya hukman). This sets the stage for the detailed discussion of definition, division, and assent in the following chapters.

Key Terms
مناظرة
نسبة تامة خبرية
مفرد
إنشاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of expression is directly debatable in munazara according to the author?
A) Simple terms (mufrad)
B) Performatives (insha')
C) Complete informative relations (nisba tamma khabariyya)
D) Inquiries (istifsar)

Key Takeaway
Only expressions that convey a truth-apt proposition (complete informative relation) are the proper subject of munazara.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the following expressions: 'Zayd is a scholar' (khabar), 'What is the time?' (istifsar), 'The prayer is obligatory' (khabar), 'I divorce you' (insha'). Which are suitable for munazara? Explain why.
?
Find an example of a performative utterance in fiqh that implies an informative claim. Rephrase it as a khabar and identify the underlying debate.

The Three Chapters of Munazara: Why Not Four?
Author sets up three chapters and addresses the objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reasoning behind the division of munazara into three chapters (definition, division, assent) and why the deficient compound is not a separate chapter.

Core Idea
The deficient compound, when qualifying a proposition, is subsumed under assent (tasdiq), so only three chapters are needed.

After excluding mufrad and insha', the author sets up three chapters for the remaining categories: definition, division, and assent. An objection is raised: why not four? The commentator resolves this by showing that the deficient compound (murakkab naqis) either qualifies a proposition (making it part of assent) or is not debatable at all.

Guided Path
1
List the four potential categories after excluding mufrad and insha'
The remaining are: definition, division, deficient compound, and assent.
2
Understand the objection
One might expect a fourth chapter for the deficient compound.
3
Examine the answer
The deficient compound, if it qualifies a proposition (e.g., 'the standing Zayd'), is considered a tasdiq in meaning; if it does not qualify, it is like mufrad or insha' and not debatable.
4
Conclude the three chapters
Thus, the author only needs three: definition (tasawwur), division (tasawwur), and assent (tasdiq). The deficient compound is covered within assent when it is a qualifier.

Types of Definition: Verbal, Attention-Drawing, and Real
Author defines ta'rif and its types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any definition as lafzi, tanbihi, or haqiqi, and identify real definitions as hadd tamm, hadd naqis, or rasm tamm.

Core Idea
Real definition captures essence; verbal explains words; attention-drawing recalls an image.

The first chapter of munazara deals with definition (ta'rif). The author distinguishes three kinds: verbal (lafzi) which explains the meaning of a word; attention-drawing (tanbihi) which retrieves a stored image; and real (haqiqi) which yields conception of the thing. Real definition is further divided into complete definition (proximate genus + differentia), deficient definition (remote genus + proximate differentia), and complete description (genus + something else).

Guided Path
1
Determine the purpose of the definition
Is it explaining a word, recalling an image, or defining the essence?
2
If real definition, extract genus (jins) and differentia (fasl)
Identify the broader category and the distinguishing feature.
3
Check proximity of genus
Is the genus the immediate (proximate) or remote (distant)?
4
Classify as hadd tamm, hadd naqis, or rasm tamm
Use the combination of genus and differentia to classify.

(And we shall begin) i.e., it is incumbent upon us to begin, and it is permissible that the lam is for inception in explaining munazara, which is the description of the two disputants on the assumption of non-transmission. He gave it precedence over the former because of its prevalence and the abundance of its investigations. (And know that the last two) i.e., the simple and the performative (here there is predominance) (munazara is not possible in them) because the subject matter of munazara is the complete informative relation, in reality or in effect; the simple has no relation at all, and the performative, although it has a complete relation, it is not informative. And the intention is that munazara does not concern the complete relation understood from the performative by primary signification; thus it does not conflict with its being concerned with the complete informative relation necessary for all performatives. As for the question in the sense of inquiry, it is not included in munazara. And since munazara is not possible in them, we lay down three chapters—each chapter for explaining the functions of one of the three matters. For if you say: it is necessary to say four chapters, because besides the last two there are four things. I say: the deficient compound, if it is a qualifier of the proposition, is a tasdiq in meaning; otherwise, munazara does not apply to it, like the simple and the performative. Chapter One: On Definition, i.e., in explaining the investigations related to definition, because the author is intending to explain the functions of definition, and the states of definition are mentioned by way of subsidiary. And it is either verbal, or attention-drawing, or real. The verbal is that by which the interpretation of the meaning of the word is intended; the attention-drawing is that by which the retrieval of a form stored in the treasury of imagination is intended without attaining to new acquisition; and the real is that whose conception entails the conception of the thing. And it is either a complete definition, which is composed of the proximate genus and difference; or a deficient definition, which is composed of the remote genus and the proximate difference; or a complete description, which is composed of the genus... (And we shall begin in explaining munazara on the assumption of non-transmission) from the person and the book, so memorize it, you will be among those of understanding. (And know that the last two), which are the simple and the performative, (munazara is possible in them) because the subject matter of munazara is the complete informative relation, in reality or in effect, as you have known, except that since it is not realized except by the realization of the two sides, they consider the locus of munazara to be the whole. And the simple has no relation at all, and the performative has a complete relation but it is not informative, neither in reality nor in effect. And there is a consideration: because the performative may have a complete informative relation in effect, as when you say, 'Someone, when he reads something, do not read the Qur'an while in a state of hadath (ritual impurity)' as if you claimed that what is read is the Qur'an, and the reader is in a state of hadath, and the impermissibility of the hadath-person reading the Qur'an; so he can deny that what is read is the Qur'an, and that he is in a state of hadath, and the impermissibility of the hadath-person reading the Qur'an. (So we lay down three chapters) for explaining the munazara that takes place in the first three: namely definition, division, and assent. He said in the gloss: If you say: it is necessary to have four chapters, I say: the deficient compound, if it is a qualifier of the proposition, is a tasdiq in meaning; but if it is not a qualifier, munazara does not apply to it, like the simple and the performative. And you have known the discussion about the performative and similarly the discussion about its qualifier. If you say: definition and division are from the category of conceptions, so they have no complete informative relation, neither in reality nor in effect, but rather a form, so munazara is not possible in them. I say: Yes, they are from the category of conceptions, but since each of them is conditioned by conditions, their relation becomes a complete informative relation in effect, so consider. (Chapter One) in explaining serious munazara (in real definition), which is that which necessarily entails, by way of examination, the distinguishing of the thing with all its individuals from all other than it, according to the later scholars, and absolutely according to... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a methodological preface to the section on munazara (dialectical debate). The commentator explains that munazara deals with complete informative relations (nisba tamma khabariyya). The simple expression (mufrad) has no relation, so it cannot be debated. The performative (insha') has a complete relation but it is not informative (khabari), so it too is excluded from munazara, unless it implies an informative claim (as when a prohibition implies an assertion of impermissibility). There is an apparent contradiction: first it says munazara is not possible in the last two, then later it says it is possible. The commentator reconciles by pointing out that performatives can have informative import in effect (hukman). The author then states that we lay down three chapters (abwab) for the first three categories (definition, division, and assent) because the fourth (deficient compound) is either a qualifier to a proposition (making it a tasdiq) or not a subject of debate. The first chapter is on definition (ta'rif). Definition is divided into verbal (lafzi), attention-drawing (tanbihi), and real (haqiqi). The verbal merely explains the meaning of a word; the attention-drawing retrieves a stored image; the real definition yields the conception of the thing. Real definition is further subdivided into complete definition (hadd tamm: proximate genus + proximate difference), deficient definition (hadd naqis: remote genus + proximate difference), and complete description (rasm tamm: composed of genus + proximate? Actually it says 'composed of genus' and cuts off). The passage also discusses the seeming objection that definition and division are conceptual (tasawwuri) and not informative propositions, so they would not be suitable for munazara. The answer is that they are conditioned by requirements (shurut) that make them effectively informative (tamma khabariyya hukman). This sets the stage for the detailed discussion of definition, division, and assent in the following chapters.

لفظي
تنبهي
حقيقي
حد تام
حد ناقص
رسم تام

B) Hadd naqis
C) Rasm tamm

Key Takeaway
Real definitions are either complete (proximate genus+differential), deficient (remote genus+proximate differential), or descriptive (genus+other).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Classify the following definitions: (1) 'Salah is the act of worship comprising specific actions and words beginning with takbir and ending with taslim' – is this hadd or rasm? (2) 'Khal is the garment worn under armor' – is this lafzi or haqiqi?
?
Provide a real definition of 'sawm' (fasting) using proximate genus and differentia. Then state whether it is a hadd tamm or hadd naqis.

The Two Duties of the Questioner in Dialectic
Author explains the three ways to refute a definition: lack of comprehensiveness, exclusiveness, or leading to absurdity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mu'aradah (objection by alternative definition) and naqd (refutation of a definition) and identify the appropriate context for each.

Core Idea
A questioner can either attack a definition by offering a better one or by showing it fails definitional conditions.

In dialectical reasoning, when a definition is proposed, the questioner (sa'il) is not passive. The text assigns two explicit duties: mu'aradah (objection by presenting an alternative definition) and naqd (refutation by pointing out flaws). Understanding these roles is essential for structured debate in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two duties
Find in the passage the two functions of the questioner: mu'aradah and naqd. Note their Arabic names.
2
Understand mu'aradah
Mu'aradah means to present a counter-definition. The questioner does not simply reject the definiens but offers a rival definition.
This is a constructive objection.
3
Understand naqd
Naqd means to refute the definition by showing it fails the conditions of jami' (comprehensiveness), mani' (exclusiveness), or leads to absurdity.
4
Apply to an example
Consider a definition: 'Salah is bowing and prostrating.' Is this a good definition? Could you use mu'aradah or naqd? See the difference.
Mu'aradah would propose a better definition; naqd would point out it excludes takbir or includes only two components.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السائل عن التعريف الحقيقي وظيفتان: إحداهما المعارضة وتسمى معارضة على التعريف، والأخرى أن ينقضه ويسمى نقض التعريف. ومعناه أن يبطله السائل بأحد أمور ثلاثة: بعدم جمعه لأفراد المعرف: أي بعدم صدقه على ما صدق عليه المعرف، أو بعدم منعه عن أغيار المعرف: أي بصدقه على ما لا يصدق عليه المعرف، أو باستلزامه المحال كالدور والتسلسل وكون الشيء ظرفا لنفسه وسلب الشيء عن نفسه واجتماع النقيضين وارتفاعهما أو غير ذلك من المحالات. قال في الحاشية: إن قلت هذا المعنى غير جامع لعدم شموله إبطاله لعدم كونه أجلى من المعرف. قلت ذلك نادر الوقوع وأطلق هنا ذكر الصور المشهورة.
The questioner concerning the real definition has two functions: one is al-mu'aradah (objection) and it is called objection against definition, and the other is to refute it (naqd) and it is called refutation of definition. Its meaning is that the questioner refutes it by one of three things: [1] by its not encompassing all individuals of the defined, i.e., its not being true of what the defined is true of; [2] or by its not excluding other things from the defined, i.e., its being true of what the defined is not true of; [3] or by its implying an absurdity, such as circularity, infinite regress, a thing being a container for itself, negation of a thing from itself, conjunction of two contradictories or their negation, or other absurdities. He said in the gloss: If you say this meaning is not comprehensive because it does not include refutation by the definition not being clearer than the defined, I say: that is rare in occurrence, and here he mentioned the well-known forms.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage explains the duties of the questioner (sa'il) when faced with a real definition. The questioner has two options: mu'aradah (objection by presenting an alternative definition) and naqd (refutation). Naqd is detailed as refuting the definition by one of three methods: (1) the definition does not include all cases of the defined (lack of comprehensiveness, jami'), (2) the definition includes things that are not the defined (lack of exclusiveness, mani'), or (3) the definition leads to logical absurdities like circularity (dawr), infinite regress (tasalsul), a thing being a container for itself (zarfiyya li nafsihi), negation of a thing from itself (salbu al-shay' 'an nafsihi), affirmation and negation of two contradictories (ijtima' al-naqidayn) or their mutual negation (irtifa'uhuma), among others. The author then addresses an objection: what about refutation based on the definition not being clearer (ajla) than the defined? He responds that such cases are rare, so only the common forms are mentioned.

Key Terms
نقض (naqḍ): refutation of a definition by showing it fails to cover all, excludes other, or implies absurdity
معارضة (mu'āraḍa): objection to a definition by presenting an alternative definition
جامع (jāmi'): condition that a definition must include all individuals of the defined
مانع (māni'): condition that a definition must exclude all individuals not of the defined

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between mu'aradah and naqd?
A) Mu'aradah is refuting the definition, naqd is offering an alternative.
B) Mu'aradah is offering an alternative definition, naqd is refuting the definition.
C) Both are the same.
D) Mu'aradah is done by the responder, naqd by the questioner.

Key Takeaway
The questioner has two weapons: offering a better definition (mu'aradah) or showing the definition fails (naqd).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are debating the definition of 'zina' (unlawful sexual intercourse). The opposing jurist defines it as 'sexual intercourse without a valid contract.' Construct a mu'aradah by proposing a better definition, and then a naqd by showing this definition fails to be exclusive (e.g., includes rape by a husband?).

The Three Ways to Refute a Definition (Naqd)
Author explains the three ways to refute a definition: lack of comprehensiveness, exclusiveness, or leading to absurdity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the three methods of naqd: lack of comprehensiveness, lack of exclusiveness, and leading to absurdity.

Core Idea
A definition is refuted if it fails to include all its members, fails to exclude others, or leads to absurdity.

The passage specifies three precise ways to refute a real definition. These correspond to the definitional conditions of jami' (comprehensiveness), mani' (exclusiveness), and the avoidance of logical contradiction (muhal). Mastering these tools allows you to critically evaluate any definition encountered in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Recall the three conditions
A good definition must be comprehensive (jami'), exclusive (mani'), and not lead to absurdity. Write them down.
2
Examine the first method: not comprehensive
The definition does not apply to all things the defined applies to. Example: defining 'wudu' as 'washing the hands and face' excludes wiping the head and washing the feet.
This definition fails jami'.
3
Examine the second method: not exclusive
The definition applies to things outside the defined. Example: defining 'salah' as 'an act of worship involving bowing and prostrating' also applies to certain forms of sajdah outside salah.
This definition fails mani'.
4
Examine the third method: leads to absurdity
Circularity, infinite regress, contradictions, etc. Example: defining 'ilm' as 'knowledge that is certain' leads to circularity if 'knowledge' is used.
5
Practice on a real definition
Take the definition of 'riba' as 'an increase in a loan without a condition'. Does it pass all three checks? If not, which fails?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السائل عن التعريف الحقيقي وظيفتان: إحداهما المعارضة وتسمى معارضة على التعريف، والأخرى أن ينقضه ويسمى نقض التعريف. ومعناه أن يبطله السائل بأحد أمور ثلاثة: بعدم جمعه لأفراد المعرف: أي بعدم صدقه على ما صدق عليه المعرف، أو بعدم منعه عن أغيار المعرف: أي بصدقه على ما لا يصدق عليه المعرف، أو باستلزامه المحال كالدور والتسلسل وكون الشيء ظرفا لنفسه وسلب الشيء عن نفسه واجتماع النقيضين وارتفاعهما أو غير ذلك من المحالات. قال في الحاشية: إن قلت هذا المعنى غير جامع لعدم شموله إبطاله لعدم كونه أجلى من المعرف. قلت ذلك نادر الوقوع وأطلق هنا ذكر الصور المشهورة.
The questioner concerning the real definition has two functions: one is al-mu'aradah (objection) and it is called objection against definition, and the other is to refute it (naqd) and it is called refutation of definition. Its meaning is that the questioner refutes it by one of three things: [1] by its not encompassing all individuals of the defined, i.e., its not being true of what the defined is true of; [2] or by its not excluding other things from the defined, i.e., its being true of what the defined is not true of; [3] or by its implying an absurdity, such as circularity, infinite regress, a thing being a container for itself, negation of a thing from itself, conjunction of two contradictories or their negation, or other absurdities. He said in the gloss: If you say this meaning is not comprehensive because it does not include refutation by the definition not being clearer than the defined, I say: that is rare in occurrence, and here he mentioned the well-known forms.

Commentary
This passage explains the duties of the questioner (sa'il) when faced with a real definition. The questioner has two options: mu'aradah (objection by presenting an alternative definition) and naqd (refutation). Naqd is detailed as refuting the definition by one of three methods: (1) the definition does not include all cases of the defined (lack of comprehensiveness, jami'), (2) the definition includes things that are not the defined (lack of exclusiveness, mani'), or (3) the definition leads to logical absurdities like circularity (dawr), infinite regress (tasalsul), a thing being a container for itself (zarfiyya li nafsihi), negation of a thing from itself (salbu al-shay' 'an nafsihi), affirmation and negation of two contradictories (ijtima' al-naqidayn) or their mutual negation (irtifa'uhuma), among others. He responds that such cases are rare, so only the common forms are mentioned.

Key Terms
جامع (jāmi'): condition that a definition must include all individuals of the defined
مانع (māni'): condition that a definition must exclude all individuals not of the defined
محال (muḥāl): an absurdity or logical impossibility, such as circularity or contradiction
دور (dawr): circularity, a logical fallacy where the definition presupposes what it defines
تسلسل (tasalsul): infinite regress, an endless chain of definitions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the three ways to refute a definition according to the text?
A) The definition is not comprehensive (jami')
B) The definition is not exclusive (mani')
C) The definition is too long
D) The definition leads to an absurdity

Key Takeaway
Any definition can be refuted by showing it fails to be comprehensive, exclusive, or coherent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition: 'Faith (iman) is belief in the heart.' Apply the three naqd methods to it. Which conditions does it violate? (Hint: it is not comprehensive because it excludes verbal confession; it may also lead to absurdity if belief is taken as mere assent without action?)

The Comprehensiveness of the Naqd Methods – A Dialectical Exchange
Author explains the three ways to refute a definition: lack of comprehensiveness, exclusiveness, or leading to absurdity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the completeness of the three-method classification by analyzing the gloss's objection and response.

Core Idea
The list of naqd methods is not exhaustive, but the author argues that uncommon methods are excluded for brevity.

The passage includes a gloss that questions whether the three methods are comprehensive. The objection: what about refutation by showing the definition is not clearer than the defined? The response: that is rare. This meta-dialectical exchange demonstrates how logical classifications can be challenged and defended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the gloss's objection
The gloss (hashiya) says: 'If you say this meaning is not comprehensive...' What is the missing method?
It is the definition being not clearer (ajla) than the defined.
2
Understand the objection's basis
A definition is supposed to be clearer than its definiendum. If it is not, it fails a key requirement. So why is it not listed?
3
Analyze the response
The author responds that such cases are rare (nadir al-wuqu') so only common forms are listed. Is that a valid reply?
Consider: does rarity excuse exclusion from a general rule?
4
Evaluate the debate
On one side, the objector demands completeness; on the other, the author prioritizes practical relevance. Who is right? In logic, a classification should ideally be exhaustive.
This is a real dialectical exercise.

السائل عن التعريف الحقيقي وظيفتان: إحداهما المعارضة وتسمى معارضة على التعريف، والأخرى أن ينقضه ويسمى نقض التعريف. ومعناه أن يبطله السائل بأحد أمور ثلاثة: بعدم جمعه لأفراد المعرف: أي بعدم صدقه على ما صدق عليه المعرف، أو بعدم منعه عن أغيار المعرف: أي بصدقه على ما لا يصدق عليه المعرف، أو باستلزامه المحال كالدور والتسلسل وكون الشيء ظرفا لنفسه وسلب الشيء عن نفسه واجتماع النقيضين وارتفاعهما أو غير ذلك من المحالات. قال في الحاشية: إن قلت هذا المعنى غير جامع لعدم شموله إبطاله لعدم كونه أجلى من المعرف. قلت ذلك نادر الوقوع وأطلق هنا ذكر الصور المشهورة.
The questioner concerning the real definition has two functions: one is al-mu'aradah (objection) and it is called objection against definition, and the other is to refute it (naqd) and it is called refutation of definition. Its meaning is that the questioner refutes it by one of three things: [1] by its not encompassing all individuals of the defined, i.e., its not being true of what the defined is true of; [2] or by its not excluding other things from the defined, i.e., its being true of what the defined is not true of; [3] or by its implying an absurdity, such as circularity, infinite regress, a thing being a container for itself, negation of a thing from itself, conjunction of two contradictories or their negation, or other absurdities. He said in the gloss: If you say this meaning is not comprehensive because it does not include refutation by the definition not being clearer than the defined, I say: that is rare in occurrence, and here he mentioned the well-known forms.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage explains the duties of the questioner (sa'il) when faced with a real definition. The questioner has two options: mu'aradah (objection by presenting an alternative definition) and naqd (refutation). Naqd is detailed as refuting the definition by one of three methods: (1) the definition does not include all cases of the defined (lack of comprehensiveness, jami'), (2) the definition includes things that are not the defined (lack of exclusiveness, mani'), or (3) the definition leads to logical absurdities like circularity (dawr), infinite regress (tasalsul), a thing being a container for itself (zarfiyya li nafsihi), negation of a thing from itself (salbu al-shay' 'an nafsihi), affirmation and negation of two contradictories (ijtima' al-naqidayn) or their mutual negation (irtifa'uhuma), among others. The author then addresses an objection: what about refutation based on the definition not being clearer (ajla) than the defined? He responds that such cases are rare, so only the common forms are mentioned.

Key Terms
حاشية (ḥāshiya): gloss or marginal commentary
نادر الوقوع (nādir al-wuqū'): rare in occurrence
أجلى (ajlā): clearer, more apparent

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The three ways are too many.
B) The three ways do not include the method of refutation by showing the definition is not clearer than the defined.
C) The definition should be refuted by its length.
D) The three ways are not commonly used.

Key Takeaway
The classification of naqd methods is defensible even if not exhaustive, as the author prioritizes common cases.

Dialectic -- Jadal

Dialectical Defense: Denying the Major Premise by Claiming a Verbal Definition
Author explains how the definer denies the major premise by claiming verbal definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the dialectical move of man' al-kubra with the support that the definition is verbal, and determine whether this defense is valid based on the relationship between the definiendum and the defining term.

Core Idea
A verbal definition is a dialectical escape hatch: it does not require essence.

In a debate about definitions, when an opponent shows that your definition is not comprehensive or not exclusive, you can deny the major premise of his syllogism. One powerful way to support this denial is to claim that your definition is verbal—it only explains the meaning of a word, not the thing itself. This lesson shows you how to execute that move and when it is legitimate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's attack
Determine whether the opponent is claiming lack of comprehensiveness (adam al-jam') or lack of exclusivity (adam al-man'). This determines which premise of his syllogism you need to deny.
2
Locate the major premise to deny
The major premise is the universal statement that the opponent uses to refute the definition. For example, 'Every definition that is not comprehensive is invalid' is the major premise. You will deny its universality.
The text prioritizes denying the major over the minor because the major is the mainstay of the argument.
3
Support the denial by claiming verbal definition
State that the definition is verbal (lafzi), meaning it only clarifies the meaning of a word, not the essence. This support works only if the definition and the defining term are in a relation of absolute generality/specificity or partial generality/specificity.
If the relation is divergent (mubayin), the support fails.
4
Consider bare denial as an alternative
The definer may also deny the major premise without any support (al-man' al-mujarrad). This is also valid, though less common. The author notes it is valid if the denied premise is not self-evident or inductive.

When the questioner invalidates the definition by lack of comprehensiveness or lack of exclusivity, then the definer—meaning the one who committed to its correctness whether it originated from him or not—may deny the major premise (i.e., the universality). Denial is asking for evidence for the premise of the argument. He only prioritized denial of the universality of the major over denial of the minor itself because the major is the mainstay of the argument, such that they said the conclusion is potentially contained in it. Hence the major is treated in dialectics with the treatment of approximation, and because its denial is like a preface for clarifying the divisions of definition and as a notification that it is appropriate for the responder to wait until the questioner completes his argument and finishes, then deny (with support), i.e., the state of the definer being supported by saying that the definition is verbal. And this is only correct if the definition is absolutely more specific or in some respect, or absolutely more general or in some respect. But if the definition is divergent, then supporting by it is not correct; so this support is a more specific support. Know that the definer may deny the major premise without support, and that is the bare denial, and it is also valid. So the restriction is either based on illustration or on the more common. And every definition of such status is invalid: this is the exposition of the first (defect). (Or) that this definition is a definition not exclusive of its others. And the better is 'and' instead of 'or'. He said in the gloss: 'not comprehensive of the individuals of the definiendum' is a negation of universal affirmation, and similarly 'not exclusive of its others' ends. Meaning they are equivalent to negation of universal affirmation because they are with negated predicate, since they are minor premises for the first figure. And 'every definition of this status is invalid' is the exposition of the second. As for the exposition of the refutation by entailment of absurdity, it will come if Allah wills. And as for the exposition of the remaining four forms, it is needless of explanation. And know that when the questioner invalidates the definition by lack of comprehensiveness or lack of exclusivity, then the definer may deny the universality of the major premise. He presented the explanation of denial of the major because the knowledge of its divisions leads him to it, unlike denial of the minor, so he delayed it and placed a chapter for it because it is lengthy. It was said: if the denied (premise) is not self-evident or inductive, but many dialecticians often deny a thing without support, so it was not paid attention to in the exposition of the dialectic and sufficed with stating its being valid at the end of this chapter. Comprehensive of its conditions, and it is permissible to present this argument from the straightforward conditional and others, but the former (is preferred). On page 16: 'Lafdh' (Word). So it is not objected that this explanation is deficient. And the correctness of this denial and its support is that definitions are two types: verbal definition, intended to know the meaning of the word, and it is of the type of assents according to al-Muhaqqiq al-Jurjani, and of the conceptual requirement according to al-Muhaqqiq al-Taftazani, and hadd and rasm are not conceived in it. And real definition. Know that 'real' is used in the context of definition in three meanings. First: what conveys a form not yet attained, whether by mere essentials or not, and whether after knowledge of the existence of the definiendum or not; in this sense it is opposed to verbal and demonstrative. Second: what conveys a form not yet attained by mere essentials, whether after knowledge of existence or not; in this sense it is opposed to verbal, demonstrative, and descriptive (rasmi). Third: what conveys a form not yet attained, whether by mere essentials or not, but after knowledge of existence; in this sense it is opposed to instinctive, demonstrative, and nominal. It is not said that this division is not comprehensive of its divisions due to the exclusion of demonstrative definition. For we say: this definition is of the type of dividing a part into its well-known parts. And its summary is specification of the divided concept to other than demonstrative. And it can be answered that we do not concede its exclusion from the division; why may it not enter into verbal definition by naming the word 'verbal' and its definition and not giving an example for it? Either based on illustration or sufficing with the more common. So let it be considered. And the first type is the determination of the meaning of the word defined. And what is in it of facility is not hidden. And the intended is that by which its meaning is determined by another word, which is the definition, whether it is synonymous or a compound expressing its meaning or not, clear in its indication of that meaning intended to be determined, with clarity appropriate to the listener. Like defining 'al-ghadanfar' by 'al-asad', which is a definition by synonym, and 'al-asad' is clear in its indication of the predatory animal relative to the listener, unlike 'al-ghadanfar' because it is a rare language for the predatory animal. And its right is to be by a single word, whether synonymous or more general or more specific; if the single word is not found, mention the compound intended for determination. He only restricted clarity relative to the listener because if it were not clear relative to him, it would not be a verbal definition. For example, if the listener knows the meaning of 'al-qisas' (retaliation) but does not know the meaning of 'al-qawd' (retaliation), one says 'al-qawd is al-qisas', meaning that 'al-qisas' is set for the meaning of 'al-qawd', and they are two synonymous words. If the situation were reversed, the matter would be reversed, so one says 'al-qisas is al-qawd'. Hence they said that verbal definition admits mutual interchange. And it (i.e., the determination of the meaning of a word) is the way of the people of language. And the intended by 'language' is all Arabic sciences, not the mere language. And it is permissible with the more general and the more specific, meaning that the original is with the synonymous and the equivalent compound, but it is permissible with the more general and the more specific. And the correctness of this denial is that definitions are two types: verbal, intended to know the meaning of the word, and it is of the type of assents, and hadd nor rasm are conceived in it; and real, intended to acquire a stored form or not yet attained in the mind, so the nominal definition is called a real definition in this sense, so the restriction of the division is not contradicted. And the first type is the determination of the meaning of the word for the convention by another word, whether it is synonymous with the definiendum or a compound expressing its meaning or not, clear in its indication of that meaning intended to be determined relative to the listener (the addressee). And better is to say: a word by which the meaning of another word is determined, etc. He said in the gloss: 'And this is like defining al-ghadanfar by al-asad, and this is a definition by synonym, and al-asad is clear in indication of the predatory animal relative to the listener, unlike al-ghadanfar because it is a rare language for the predatory animal.' End. And like explaining 'existence' as 'what is either an agent or a patient'. And it (i.e., determination of the meaning of a word) is the way of the people of language and Arab scholars. And this determination is permissible with the absolutely general, so it is not exclusive, and with the absolutely specific, so it is not comprehensive, so it is true.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a combination of dialectical strategy and definitional classification. It begins by describing the dialectical situation: when a questioner (sā'il) invalidates a definition by pointing out that it is either not comprehensive or not exclusive, the definer (the one who holds the definition) has the option to deny the major premise (man' al-kubrā) of the syllogism that was used to refute him. Denial (man') means demanding proof for the premise. The author notes that it is better to deny the universality of the major premise before denying the minor premise, because the major is the core of the argument, and its denial serves as a prelude to discussing the types of definitions. The definer can deny with support (mustanidan) by claiming that the definition is verbal (lafzī), i.e., it only explains the meaning of a word, not the essence. This is valid only if the definition is more specific or more general in an absolute sense or in some respect; if it is divergent (mubāyin), this support does not work. The definer may also simply deny without support (al-man' al-mujarrad), which is also considered valid, though the more common practice is to provide support. The author then reiterates the two defects with their explanations. Then, on page 16, the text turns to the classification of definitions. The support for the denial is that definitions are of two types: verbal (lafzī) and real (haqīqī). Verbal definition aims to clarify the meaning of a word, and it belongs to the realm of assents (tasdiqāt) according to al-Jurjānī, or to tasawwurī demands according to al-Taftāzānī. It does not involve true definition (hadd) or description (rasm). Real definition is then elaborated with three meanings: (1) conveying a form not yet attained, whether by essential predicates or not, regardless of prior knowledge of existence—opposed to verbal and demonstrative; (2) conveying a form not yet attained by essential predicates only—opposed to verbal, demonstrative, and descriptive; (3) conveying a form not yet attained, but only after knowledge of existence—opposed to instinctive, demonstrative, and nominal. The author addresses a potential objection that this division excludes demonstrative definition, defending it by saying that it is a division of a part into its well-known parts, i.e., it limits the divided concept to exclude demonstrative. Alternatively, one could argue that demonstrative definition might be included in verbal definition by a broader interpretation. Then the author explains the first type (verbal definition) in detail: it is the determination of the meaning of a word by another word that is clear to the listener, whether synonymous, or compound, or more general or more specific. The key is clarity to the listener; if the listener understands 'asad' better than 'ghadanfar', then defining the latter with the former is valid. This can be reversed, so verbal definitions are interchangeable. This method is the way of lexicographers. It is permissible to use a more general or more specific term, even though the ideal is a synonym or equivalent compound. The passage concludes by reiterating the correctness of the denial based on the division of definitions into verbal and real.

D) The definition must be a synonym

Key Takeaway
Denying the major premise with the support that a definition is verbal is a key dialectical tool that shifts the burden back to the opponent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In a dialectical exchange about the definition of 'riba', an opponent argues that the definition 'increase in a loan contract' is not comprehensive because it does not cover barter transactions. Show how the definer can deny the major premise by claiming the definition is verbal, and explain why this support is valid or not.

Dialectic -- Jadal
intermediate

Classification of Definitions: Verbal vs. Real and the Three Meanings of Real
Author divides definitions into verbal and real, and gives three meanings of real.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) and real definition (ta'rif haqiqi), and identify the three meanings of real definition according to al-Waldiyya.

Core Idea
Real definition has three meanings depending on whether it uses essentials and whether prior knowledge of existence is required.

The author systematically divides definitions into verbal and real. Verbal definitions only clarify the meaning of a word. Real definitions convey a form of the thing and are subdivided into three types based on what they include (essentials only or not) and whether they presume prior knowledge of existence. This lesson helps you navigate this nuanced classification.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish verbal from real definitions
A verbal definition (lafzi) aims to clarify the meaning of a word by using another word or phrase that is clearer to the listener. It belongs to the realm of assents (tasdiqat). A real definition (haqiqi) aims to convey a form of the thing itself.
Verbal definitions do not involve hadd (essential definition) or rasm (description).
2
Understand the three meanings of real definition
First meaning: conveys a new form, whether by essentials or not, and whether after knowledge of existence or not. Second meaning: conveys a new form by essentials only. Third meaning: conveys a new form (any predicates) only after knowledge of existence.
Each meaning is opposed to different types: verbal, demonstrative, descriptive, nominal, etc.
3
Address the objection about demonstrative definition
The classification excludes demonstrative definition (ta'rif tanbihi). The author defends this by saying the division is of a part into its well-known parts, or that demonstrative could be included under verbal definition.
4
Examine verbal definition in detail
Verbal definition must be clear to the listener and can use synonyms, compounds, or even more general/specific terms. It is the method of lexicographers.
The example is defining 'ghadanfar' by 'asad' (lion).
